## 1. Introduction

### 1.1 Manual Purpose

**English:**
This manual provides comprehensive instructions for warehouse staff at Smart Dairy Ltd. on using the Smart Web Portal System for daily warehouse operations. It covers all essential functions including inventory management, receiving, picking, packing, shipping, and cold chain management specific to dairy products.

| Function | Description | Bengali |

### 1.3 System Requirements

**For Desktop/Tablet:**
- Chrome 90+ or Firefox 88+ or Edge 90+
- Screen resolution: 1280x768 or higher (recommended)
- Stable internet connection
- Barcode/RFID scanner (USB or Bluetooth)

**For Mobile App:**
- Android 8.0+ or iOS 13.0+
- Camera for barcode scanning
- 50MB free storage space

---

## 2. Getting Started

### 2.1 Login Process

**Step-by-Step Instructions:**

1. **Access the Warehouse Portal**
   - URL: https://warehouse.smartdairybd.com
   - Or open Smart Dairy Warehouse mobile app

2. **Enter Credentials**
   ```
   Username: Your employee ID (e.g., WH-001234)
   Password: Your secure password
   ```

3. **Two-Factor Authentication (if enabled)**
   - Enter OTP sent to your registered mobile number
   - OTP valid for 5 minutes

4. **Select Your Shift/Location**
   ```
   Select Warehouse:
   â—‹ Main Distribution Center (Dhaka)
   â—‹ Farm Cold Storage (Rupgonj)
   â—‹ Retail Distribution Hub
   ```

**Step-by-Step: Check Product Stock**

1. **Search for Product**
   - Enter product name, code, or barcode in search box
   - Press Enter or click ğŸ” icon

2. **View Stock Details**
   - Click on product row to expand details
   - View breakdown by:
     - Location/Bin
     - Batch/Lot number
     - Expiry date
     - Reserved quantity

### 3.2 Stock Count / Physical Verification

**Purpose:**
Verify physical stock matches system records through regular cycle counts and full physical inventories.

**Types of Stock Counts:**

| Count Type | Frequency | Duration | Scope |
|------------|-----------|----------|-------|
| **Cycle Count** | Daily | 30-60 min | Selected products/locations |
| **Zone Count** | Weekly | 2-4 hours | Specific warehouse zone |
| **Full Inventory** | Monthly/Quarterly | 1-2 days | Entire warehouse |
| **Ad-hoc Count** | As needed | Varies | Specific investigation |

**Step-by-Step: Perform Cycle Count**

1. **Start Count Session**
   - Navigate to: Inventory â†’ Stock Count â†’ New Count
   - Select count type: "Cycle Count"
   - Select zone/location to count
   - Click "Start Count Session"

2. **Count Screen:**
   ```

   - Point scanner at product barcode
   - Scanner beeps and product details appear
   - Enter physical quantity counted
   - Click "Save & Continue"

4. **Handling Discrepancies:**
   - If counted qty â‰  expected qty:
     - System highlights variance
     - Enter reason code:
       - DMG - Damaged goods
       - EXP - Expired product
       - THE - Theft/Loss
       - ADJ - Adjustment error
       - OTH - Other (specify in notes)
   - Supervisor approval required for variances > 5%

5. **Complete Count Session**
   - Review all counted items
   - Submit for approval
   - System generates variance report

**Variance Report Example:**
```

### 3.3 Adjust Inventory

**When to Adjust Inventory:**
- Stock count variances
- Damaged/spoiled products
- Product returns
- System corrections
- Sample/testing withdrawals

**Step-by-Step: Create Inventory Adjustment**

1. **Navigate to Adjustment Screen**
   - Inventory â†’ Adjustments â†’ New Adjustment

2. **Fill Adjustment Form:**
   ```
   â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”

   â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜
   ```

3. **Required Information:**
   - Adjustment type (increase/decrease)
   - Reason code (mandatory)
   - Product, location, batch
   - Adjustment quantity
   - Supporting notes/photos

4. **Approval Workflow:**
   - Adjustments < 50 units: Supervisor approval
   - Adjustments 50-200 units: Warehouse Manager approval
   - Adjustments > 200 units: Operations Manager approval

**Adjustment Reason Codes:**

| Code | Reason | When to Use |
|------|--------|-------------|
| DMG | Damaged | Broken, leaking, or physically damaged products |
| EXP | Expired | Products past expiry date |
| RET | Return | Customer returns (good condition) |
| SPO | Spoilage | Temperature excursion, contamination |
| SAM | Sample | Quality testing, marketing samples |
| THE | Theft/Loss | Missing inventory, suspected theft |
| COR | Correction | Fixing system errors |
| REC | Received | Additional goods received without GRN |

   - Select source and destination locations

## 4. Receiving

### 4.1 Receive Incoming Goods

**Receiving Process Overview:**

```

5. **Complete Receipt:**
   - System generates Goods Receipt Note (GRN)
   - GRN Number format: GRN-YYYY-XXXXXX
   - Print GRN for supplier acknowledgment
   - Items moved to "QC Hold" or "Received" status

### 4.2 Quality Check at Receipt

**Quality Check Procedures:**

| Check Type | What to Verify | Accept/Reject Criteria |
|------------|----------------|------------------------|
| **Visual** | Packaging, seals, labels | No damage, tampering, or leaks |
| **Temperature** | Product and vehicle temp | Within specified range |
| **Quantity** | Physical count vs. documents | Â±2% tolerance |
| **Documentation** | COA, batch codes, expiry dates | Complete and matches |
| **Organoleptic** | Color, smell (if required) | Normal characteristics |

**Quality Check Screen:**

**Rejection Reason Codes:**

| Code | Reason | Action |
|------|--------|--------|
| TEMPHIGH | Temperature too high | Reject, notify supplier |
| TEMPLOW | Temperature too low | Check product condition |
| DAMAGE | Packaging damaged | Reject damaged units |
| SHORT | Quantity shortage | Receive partial, report |
| EXPIRED | Past expiry date | Reject all |
| WRONG | Wrong product delivered | Reject, return to supplier |
| QUALITY | Quality concerns | Quarantine for testing |

### 4.3 Put-Away Process

**Put-Away is the process of moving received goods from receiving dock to their designated storage locations.**

**Put-Away Rules:**

| Product Type | Storage Zone | Temperature | FIFO/FEFO |
|--------------|--------------|-------------|-----------|
| Fresh Milk | Cold Zone A | 2-4Â°C | FEFO |
| Yogurt | Cold Zone B | 2-6Â°C | FEFO |
| Cheese | Cold Zone C | 2-4Â°C | FEFO |
| Butter | Cold Zone B | 0-4Â°C | FEFO |
| Ice Cream | Frozen Storage | -18Â°C | FIFO |
| Dry Goods | Dry Storage | Ambient | FIFO |

**Step-by-Step: Put-Away**

1. **View Put-Away List:**
   ```
   â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”

   - Based on product type and zone rules
   - Considers available capacity
   - Optimizes for FEFO (First Expired First Out)

4. **Confirm Put-Away:**
   - System updates inventory location
   - Stock becomes available for orders
   - Task marked complete

### 4.4 Handle Returns

**Types of Returns:**

| Return Type | Source | Disposition |
|-------------|--------|-------------|
| **Customer Return** | B2B/B2C orders | QC inspection â†’ restock/reject |
| **Supplier Return** | Rejected receipt | Return to supplier |
| **Internal Return** | Transfer reversals | Return to stock |

**Step-by-Step: Process Customer Return**

1. **Access Returns Screen:**
   - Receiving â†’ Returns â†’ New Return

   ```

```

3. **Physical Inspection:**
   - Receive returned goods at warehouse
   - QC inspection for condition
   - Determine disposition:
     - Restock (if good condition)
     - Destroy (if damaged/expired)
     - Return to supplier

4. **Complete Return:**
   - System updates inventory
   - Credit note generated for customer
   - Return merchandise authorized (RMA) closed

## 5. Picking & Packing

### 5.1 Pick List Generation

**Pick List is a document/instruction that tells warehouse staff which products to pick, in what quantity, and from which locations.**

**Types of Picking:**

| Pick Type | Description | Best For |
|-----------|-------------|----------|
| **Order Picking** | Pick items for single order | Small orders, B2C |
| **Batch Picking** | Pick multiple orders together | High volume, similar products |
| **Zone Picking** | Pick from assigned zone only | Large warehouses |
| **Wave Picking** | Pick by schedule waves | Scheduled deliveries |

**Pick List Generation Screen:**

```

```

3. **Pick Verification:**
   - Scan location barcode (confirms you're at right place)
   - Scan product barcode (confirms right product)
   - Enter quantity picked
   - System validates against pick list

4. **Handle Pick Issues:**

| Issue | Action | System Entry |
|-------|--------|--------------|
| Item not found | Search alternative location | Mark as "Not Found" |
| Insufficient stock | Pick available, short pick | Enter actual qty |
| Damaged product | Pick alternate batch | Note damage reason |
| Wrong batch | Pick FEFO batch | Scan correct batch |

**Batch Picking Process:**
- Pick all items for multiple orders together
- Sort by location to minimize travel
- Place items in totes/carts labeled by order
- Consolidate at packing station

**à¦¬à¦¾à¦‚à¦²à¦¾:**
à¦ªà¦¿à¦•à¦¿à¦‚ à¦•à¦°à¦¤à§‡ à¦²à§‹à¦•à§‡à¦¶à¦¨ à¦à¦¬à¦‚ à¦ªà¦£à§à¦¯à§‡à¦° à¦¬à¦¾à¦°à¦•à§‹à¦¡ à¦¸à§à¦•à§à¦¯à¦¾à¦¨ à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤ à¦ªà¦°à¦¿à¦®à¦¾à¦£ à¦²à¦¿à¦–à§à¦¨ à¦à¦¬à¦‚ à¦¨à¦¿à¦¶à§à¦šà¦¿à¦¤ à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤ à¦¸à¦®à¦¸à§à¦¯à¦¾ à¦¹à¦²à§‡ "à¦¨à¦Ÿ à¦«à¦¾à¦‰à¦¨à§à¦¡" à¦¬à¦¾ "à¦¶à¦°à§à¦Ÿ à¦ªà¦¿à¦•" à¦šà¦¿à¦¹à§à¦¨à¦¿à¦¤ à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤ à¦¬à§à¦¯à¦¾à¦š à¦ªà¦¿à¦•à¦¿à¦‚à¦¯à¦¼à§‡ à¦à¦•à¦¸à¦¾à¦¥à§‡ à¦à¦•à¦¾à¦§à¦¿à¦• à¦…à¦°à§à¦¡à¦¾à¦° à¦¬à¦¾à¦›à¦¾à¦‡ à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤

2. **Cold Chain Packing Requirements:**

| Product | Packaging | Cold Packs | Temp Monitor |
|---------|-----------|------------|--------------|
| Fresh Milk | Insulated box | 2-4 gel packs | Required |
| Yogurt | Insulated box | 2-3 gel packs | Required |
| Cheese | Insulated box | 1-2 gel packs | Required |
| Butter | Insulated box | 1-2 gel packs | Required |
| Ice Cream | Dry ice box | Dry ice | Required |

3. **Packing Verification:**
   - Count items against pick list
   - Verify product condition
   - Select appropriate packaging
   - Add required cold packs
   - Attach temperature logger (for cold chain)
   - Seal package securely
   - Apply shipping label

**à¦¬à¦¾à¦‚à¦²à¦¾:**
à¦ªà§à¦¯à¦¾à¦•à¦¿à¦‚ à¦•à¦°à¦¤à§‡ à¦¬à¦¾à¦›à¦¾à¦‡à¦•à§ƒà¦¤ à¦†à¦‡à¦Ÿà§‡à¦® à¦¯à¦¾à¦šà¦¾à¦‡ à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨, à¦ªà§à¦¯à¦¾à¦•à§‡à¦œà¦¿à¦‚ à¦¨à¦¿à¦°à§à¦¬à¦¾à¦šà¦¨ à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨, à¦à¦¬à¦‚ à¦ à¦¾à¦¨à§à¦¡à¦¾ à¦šà§‡à¦‡à¦¨à§‡à¦° à¦œà¦¨à§à¦¯ à¦œà§‡à¦² à¦ªà§à¦¯à¦¾à¦• à¦¯à§‹à¦— à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤ à¦¤à¦¾à¦ªà¦®à¦¾à¦¤à§à¦°à¦¾ à¦²à¦—à¦¾à¦° à¦¸à¦‚à¦¯à§à¦•à§à¦¤ à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤ à¦“à¦œà¦¨ à¦®à¦¾à¦ªà§à¦¨ à¦à¦¬à¦‚ à¦²à§‡à¦¬à§‡à¦² à¦ªà§à¦°à¦¿à¦¨à§à¦Ÿ à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤

### 5.4 Label Printing

**Types of Labels:**

| Label Type | Purpose | Information |
|------------|---------|-------------|
| **Product Label** | Individual item identification | SKU, batch, expiry, barcode |
| **Pallet Label** | Bulk storage identification | Contents, qty, location |
| **Shipping Label** | Delivery identification | Address, order #, barcode |
| **Cold Chain Label** | Temperature requirements | Temp range, handling instructions |
| **Hazmat Label** | Special handling | Warning symbols, instructions |

**Label Printing Screen:**

```

**Label Placement Guidelines:**
- Shipping label: Top right corner, clearly visible
- Cold chain label: Multiple sides for visibility
- Fragile stickers: Near shipping label
- This-way-up arrows: Both sides of package

## 6. Shipping

### 6.1 Create Delivery Notes

**Delivery Note (DN) is a document that accompanies the shipment, listing all items being delivered.**

**Step-by-Step: Create Delivery Note**

1. **Access Shipping Screen:**
   - Shipping â†’ Create Delivery â†’ Select Orders

2. **Select Packed Orders:**
   ```

3. **System Generates Delivery Note:**
   - DN Number format: DN-YYYY-XXXXXX
   - Includes all order details
   - Barcode for tracking
   - Temperature requirements

4. **Print Loading Sheet:**
   - Lists all packages by stop order
   - Shows weight and dimensions
   - Driver signature section

**Delivery Note Format:**
```

### 6.2 Assign to Logistics

**Vehicle Assignment:**

| Vehicle Type | Capacity | Temperature | Best For |
|--------------|----------|-------------|----------|
| Refrigerated Van (Small) | 500 kg | 0-4Â°C | Small orders, city delivery |
| Refrigerated Van (Large) | 2000 kg | 0-4Â°C | Bulk orders, B2B |
| Refrigerated Truck | 5000 kg | -18 to +4Â°C | Large distribution |
| Motorcycle with Cool Box | 50 kg | 2-8Â°C | Urgent small orders |

### 6.4 Proof of Delivery

**Delivery Completion Process:**

1. **Driver Scans Delivery Note** at customer location
2. **Customer Verification:**
   - Count packages
   - Check condition
   - Verify temperature (if required)
3. **Digital Signature** captured on driver device
4. **Photo** of delivered goods (optional)
5. **System Updates:**
   - Delivery marked complete
   - Timestamp recorded
   - Customer notification sent

**Proof of Delivery Screen:**

```

## 7. Cold Chain Management

### 7.1 Temperature Monitoring

**Critical Temperature Ranges:**

| Product | Storage Temp | Transport Temp | Alert Threshold |
|---------|--------------|----------------|-----------------|
| Fresh Milk | 0-4Â°C | 0-4Â°C | > 4Â°C for > 30 min |
| Yogurt | 2-6Â°C | 2-6Â°C | > 6Â°C for > 30 min |
| Cheese | 2-4Â°C | 2-4Â°C | > 4Â°C for > 30 min |
| Butter | 0-4Â°C | 0-4Â°C | > 4Â°C for > 30 min |
| Ice Cream | -18Â°C | -18Â°C | > -12Â°C for > 10 min |

**Temperature Monitoring Dashboard:**

**Zone Access Rules:**

| Zone | Products | Max Door Open | Access Level |
|------|----------|---------------|--------------|
| Zone A | Fresh milk, mattha | 5 minutes | All warehouse staff |
| Zone B | Yogurt, butter | 5 minutes | All warehouse staff |
| Zone C | Cheese, cream | 5 minutes | All warehouse staff |
| Zone D | Returns, overflow | 10 minutes | Supervisor+ |
| Dock Chill | Staging | 15 minutes | All warehouse staff |
| Freezer | Ice cream | 5 minutes | Authorized only |

**Zone Transfer Procedure:**
1. Check destination zone capacity
2. Verify temperature compatibility
3. Update system with new location
4. Complete transfer within 10 minutes
5. Verify temperature maintained

à¦•à§‹à¦²à§à¦¡ à¦¸à§à¦Ÿà§‹à¦°à§‡à¦œ à¦œà§‹à¦¨à§‡ à¦ªà§à¦°à¦¬à§‡à¦¶à§‡à¦° à¦¸à¦®à¦¯à¦¼ à¦¦à¦°à¦œà¦¾ à§« à¦®à¦¿à¦¨à¦¿à¦Ÿà§‡à¦° à¦¬à§‡à¦¶à¦¿ à¦–à§‹à¦²à¦¾ à¦°à¦¾à¦–à¦¬à§‡à¦¨ à¦¨à¦¾à¥¤ à¦œà§‹à¦¨à§‡à¦° à¦®à¦§à§à¦¯à§‡ à¦¸à§à¦Ÿà§‹à¦• à¦¸à¦°à¦¾à¦¤à§‡ à§§à§¦ à¦®à¦¿à¦¨à¦¿à¦Ÿà§‡à¦° à¦®à¦§à§à¦¯à§‡ à¦¸à¦®à§à¦ªà§‚à¦°à§à¦£ à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤ à¦…à¦¨à¦¨à§à¦®à§‹à¦¦à¦¿à¦¤ à¦¬à§à¦¯à¦•à§à¦¤à¦¿ à¦«à§à¦°à¦¿à¦œà¦¾à¦° à¦œà§‹à¦¨à§‡ à¦ªà§à¦°à¦¬à§‡à¦¶ à¦•à¦°à¦¤à§‡ à¦ªà¦¾à¦°à¦¬à§‡ à¦¨à¦¾à¥¤

### 7.3 FIFO/FEFO Compliance

**FIFO (First In First Out)** - Used for products with same expiry
**FEFO (First Expired First Out)** - Used for products with different expiry dates (Dairy standard)

**FEFO Compliance Procedures:**

1. **Receiving:**
   - Record batch number and expiry date
   - System assigns FEFO priority
   - Place in designated zone location

2. **Picking:**
   - System suggests oldest expiry first
   - Verify batch on pick list
   - If older batch exists, pick that instead

3. **Stock Rotation:**
   - Weekly rotation checks
   - Move older stock to front
   - Mark near-expiry items

**FEFO Report:**

```
â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”

| Alert Level | Trigger | Action Required |

### 8.2 Expiry Alerts

**Expiry Alert Timeline:**

| Days to Expiry | Alert Level | Action |
|----------------|-------------|--------|
| 0-3 days | ğŸ”´ Critical | Expedite sales, prepare disposal |
| 4-7 days | ğŸŸ  High | Promote sales, discount if needed |
| 8-14 days | ğŸŸ¡ Medium | Monitor, plan promotions |
| 15-30 days | ğŸŸ¢ Low | Normal monitoring |

### 8.3 Reorder Points

**Reorder Point Calculation:**
```
Reorder Point = (Average Daily Usage Ã— Lead Time) + Safety Stock
```

## 9. Reports

### 9.1 Stock Reports

**Available Stock Reports:**

| Report | Description | Frequency |
|--------|-------------|-----------|
| **Current Stock** | Real-time inventory snapshot | On demand |
| **Stock Movement** | In/out transactions | Daily/Weekly |
| **Stock Valuation** | Inventory value by product | Monthly |
| **Slow Moving** | Items with low turnover | Monthly |
| **Stock Aging** | Time in inventory analysis | Weekly |

### 9.2 Movement History

**Movement Types:**

| Type | Code | Description |
|------|------|-------------|
| Receipt | RC | Goods received from supplier |
| Issue | IS | Goods issued to production/customer |
| Transfer | TR | Internal location transfer |
| Adjustment | AD | Inventory adjustment |
| Return | RT | Customer/supplier return |
| Conversion | CV | Unit of measure conversion |

## 10. Barcode/RFID Scanning

### 10.1 Scan Procedures

**Supported Barcode Types:**

| Type | Use Case | Example |
|------|----------|---------|
| **Code 128** | Product identification | SD-MILK-001 |
| **QR Code** | Batch/location tracking | Batch details |
| **Data Matrix** | Small item marking | Unit level |
| **EAN-13** | Consumer products | 894123456789 |

**Scanning Best Practices:**

1. **Positioning:**
   - Hold scanner 10-20 cm from barcode
   - Align laser/camera with barcode
   - Ensure good lighting
   - Avoid glare on glossy surfaces

2. **Verification:**
   - Listen for beep confirmation
   - Check screen for correct data
   - If failed, try different angle
   - Clean scanner lens if persistent issues

3. **Common Scanning Issues:**

| Issue | Cause | Solution |
|-------|-------|----------|
| No beep | Scanner not connected | Check cable/Bluetooth |
| Wrong data | Damaged barcode | Enter manually |
| Multiple beeps | Duplicate scan | Wait between scans |
| Slow response | Low battery | Charge/replace battery |

**Scan Workflows:**

**Receiving Scan:**
```
1. Scan Purchase Order barcode
2. Scan product barcode
3. Enter quantity
4. Scan storage location
5. Confirm
```

**Picking Scan:**
```
1. Scan Pick List barcode
2. Scan location barcode (verify position)
3. Scan product barcode (verify item)
4. Enter quantity picked
5. Confirm and continue
```

**Shipping Scan:**
```
1. Scan Delivery Note
2. Scan each package barcode
3. Verify against list
4. Complete loading
```

**à¦¬à¦¾à¦‚à¦²à¦¾:**
à¦¸à§à¦•à§à¦¯à¦¾à¦¨ à¦•à¦°à¦¤à§‡ à§§à§¦-à§¨à§¦ à¦¸à§‡à¦®à¦¿ à¦¦à§‚à¦°à¦¤à§à¦¬à§‡ à¦§à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤ à¦¬à¦¿à¦ª à¦•à¦°à§‡ à¦¸à¦ à¦¿à¦• à¦¤à¦¥à§à¦¯ à¦¦à§‡à¦–à§à¦¨à¥¤ à¦¸à¦®à¦¸à§à¦¯à¦¾ à¦¹à¦²à§‡ à¦®à§à¦¯à¦¾à¦¨à§à¦¯à¦¼à¦¾à¦²à¦¿ à¦à¦¨à§à¦Ÿà§à¦°à¦¿ à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤

## 11. Mobile App - Warehouse Features

### 11.1 Mobile App Overview

**App Name:** Smart Dairy Warehouse Mobile
**Platforms:** Android, iOS

**Key Features:**
- Real-time inventory lookup
- Barcode scanning using phone camera
- Picking and put-away workflows
- Stock count support
- Temperature logging
- Offline mode for cold storage areas

**Mobile Screen Examples:**

### 11.2 Offline Mode

**When to Use Offline Mode:**
- Cold storage areas with poor WiFi
- During network outages
- Remote locations

**How It Works:**
1. Data synced when connected
2. Actions queued when offline
3. Auto-sync when connection restored
4. Conflict resolution for simultaneous edits

**Offline Capabilities:**
- View cached inventory data
- Record stock counts
- Complete pick tasks
- Log temperature readings

**Sync Status:**
```

## 12. Safety Procedures

### 12.1 Cold Storage Safety

**âš ï¸ DANGER: Cold storage areas pose serious health and safety risks. Follow all procedures carefully.**

**Cold Storage Hazards:**

| Hazard | Risk | Prevention |
|--------|------|------------|
| Hypothermia | Body temperature drop | Limit exposure time |
| Frostbite | Skin tissue damage | Proper PPE, no bare skin |
| Slips/Falls | Wet/icy floors | Anti-slip footwear, walk carefully |
| Entrapment | Locked inside | Emergency alarms, buddy system |
| Equipment | Moving machinery | Training, lockout procedures |

**Cold Storage PPE (Personal Protective Equipment):**

```
â”Œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”
â”‚  COLD STORAGE PPE REQUIREMENTS                                              â”‚
â”œâ”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”¤
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  REQUIRED FOR ENTRY (Zone A, B, C - 2-4Â°C):                                 â”‚
â”‚  â˜‘ï¸ Insulated jacket (provided)                                             â”‚
â”‚  â˜‘ï¸ Thermal gloves                                                          â”‚
â”‚  â˜‘ï¸ Closed-toe shoes with grip                                              â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  REQUIRED FOR FREEZER (-18Â°C):                                              â”‚
â”‚  â˜‘ï¸ Full cold storage suit                                                  â”‚
â”‚  â˜‘ï¸ Insulated boots                                                         â”‚
â”‚  â˜‘ï¸ Thermal gloves                                                          â”‚
â”‚  â˜‘ï¸ Face protection                                                         â”‚
â”‚  â˜‘ï¸ Hard hat                                                                â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  MAXIMUM EXPOSURE TIMES:                                                    â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ 2-4Â°C zones: 2 hours continuous                                          â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ -18Â°C freezer: 30 minutes continuous                                     â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  MANDATORY BREAKS:                                                          â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ 15 min break after 1 hour in 2-4Â°C                                       â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ 30 min break after 30 min in -18Â°C                                       â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  EMERGENCY PROCEDURES:                                                      â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Emergency alarm button at each door                                      â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Emergency phone inside each zone                                         â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Trapped inside: Press alarm, stay near door, help will come              â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Medical emergency: Call extension 911, move person to warm area          â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â””â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”˜
```

**Cold Storage Entry Procedure:**

1. **Before Entering:**
   - Check you have proper PPE
   - Inform supervisor of entry
   - Check emergency alarm is working
   - Note entry time

2. **During Work:**
   - Stay alert for cold symptoms
   - Watch for slippery floors
   - Keep door closed when not entering/exiting
   - Work efficiently to minimize exposure

3. **Emergency Situations:**
   - Door won't open: Press alarm button
   - Feeling dizzy/cold: Exit immediately
   - Colleague unresponsive: Call emergency, move to warm area

**à¦¬à¦¾à¦‚à¦²à¦¾:**
à¦•à§‹à¦²à§à¦¡ à¦¸à§à¦Ÿà§‹à¦°à§‡à¦œà§‡ à¦ªà§à¦°à¦¬à§‡à¦¶à§‡à¦° à¦†à¦—à§‡ PPE à¦ªà¦°à§à¦¨ à¦à¦¬à¦‚ à¦¸à§à¦ªà¦¾à¦°à¦­à¦¾à¦‡à¦œà¦¾à¦°à¦•à§‡ à¦œà¦¾à¦¨à¦¾à¦¨à¥¤ à¦¸à¦°à§à¦¬à¦¾à¦§à¦¿à¦• à¦à¦•à§à¦¸à¦ªà§‹à¦œà¦¾à¦° à¦¸à¦®à¦¯à¦¼ à¦®à§‡à¦¨à§‡ à¦šà¦²à§à¦¨à¥¤ à¦œà¦°à§à¦°à¦¿ à¦…à§à¦¯à¦¾à¦²à¦¾à¦°à§à¦® à¦¬à¦¾à¦Ÿà¦¨ à¦¬à§à¦¯à¦¬à¦¹à¦¾à¦° à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤

### 12.2 Material Handling Safety

**Manual Handling Guidelines:**

| Item Weight | Handling Method |
|-------------|-----------------|
| < 10 kg | Single person, proper lifting |
| 10-20 kg | Single person, use correct technique |
| 20-25 kg | Two persons or mechanical aid |
| > 25 kg | Mechanical aid required (trolley, forklift) |

**Lifting Technique:**
```
SAFE LIFTING TECHNIQUE
â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•

1. PLAN THE LIFT
   - Check path is clear
   - Know where you're going
   - Get help if needed

2. POSITION YOURSELF
   - Stand close to load
   - Feet shoulder-width apart
   - One foot slightly forward

3. BEND YOUR KNEES
   - Keep back straight
   - Squat down to load
   - Do NOT bend at waist

4. GRIP FIRMLY
   - Use both hands
   - Grip opposite corners
   - Ensure secure hold

5. LIFT SMOOTHLY
   - Straighten legs
   - Keep load close to body
   - Do not twist while lifting

6. CARRY CAREFULLY
   - Keep load at waist height
   - Watch where you're going
   - Set down using same technique
```

**Equipment Safety:**

| Equipment | Training Required | Safety Checks |
|-----------|-------------------|---------------|
| Pallet Jack | Basic induction | Wheels, brakes, forks |
| Forklift | Certified license | Daily checklist |
| Trolley | Basic induction | Wheels, handles |
| Conveyor | Job specific | Emergency stops |

**à¦¬à¦¾à¦‚à¦²à¦¾:**
à¦­à¦¾à¦°à§€ à¦¬à¦¸à§à¦¤à§ à¦¤à§‹à¦²à¦¾à¦° à¦¸à¦®à¦¯à¦¼ à¦¸à¦ à¦¿à¦• à¦•à§Œà¦¶à¦² à¦¬à§à¦¯à¦¬à¦¹à¦¾à¦° à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤ à§¨à§« à¦•à§‡à¦œà¦¿à¦° à¦¬à§‡à¦¶à¦¿ à¦®à§‡à¦•à¦¾à¦¨à¦¿à¦•à§à¦¯à¦¾à¦² à¦¸à¦¾à¦¹à¦¾à¦¯à§à¦¯ à¦¬à§à¦¯à¦¬à¦¹à¦¾à¦° à¦•à¦°à§à¦¨à¥¤ à¦¸à¦°à¦à§à¦œà¦¾à¦® à¦¬à§à¦¯à¦¬à¦¹à¦¾à¦°à§‡à¦° à¦†à¦—à§‡ à¦Ÿà§à¦°à§‡à¦¨à¦¿à¦‚ à¦¨à¦¿à¦¨à¥¤

### 12.3 Emergency Procedures

**Emergency Contacts:**

| Emergency | Number/Contact |
|-----------|----------------|
| Fire | 999 or extension 911 |
| Medical | Extension 912 or 017XXXXXXXX |
| Security | Extension 913 |
| Warehouse Manager | 017XXXXXXXX |
| IT Support | Extension 888 |

**Emergency Procedures:**

**Fire:**
1. Activate nearest fire alarm
2. Evacuate immediately via nearest exit
3. Do not use elevators
4. Assembly point: Main parking lot
5. Report to supervisor for headcount

**Medical Emergency:**
1. Call for help (extension 912)
2. Do not move injured person unless immediate danger
3. Provide first aid if trained
4. Clear area for medical personnel
5. Document incident

**Chemical Spill:**
1. Evacuate area immediately
2. Alert supervisor
3. Do not attempt cleanup unless trained
4. Follow posted spill procedures

**Power Outage:**
1. Stop all machinery safely
2. Emergency lights will activate
3. Wait for instructions from supervisor
4. Do not enter cold storage during outage

## 13. Troubleshooting

### 13.1 Common Issues

| Issue | Possible Cause | Solution |
|-------|---------------|----------|
| Can't login | Wrong password | Reset password via "Forgot Password" |
| | Account locked | Contact supervisor/IT |
| Page not loading | Internet issue | Check connection, refresh |
| | System maintenance | Wait or contact IT |
| Barcode not scanning | Damaged barcode | Enter manually |
| | Scanner issue | See scanner troubleshooting |
| Wrong stock showing | Sync delay | Wait 2 minutes, refresh |
| | Another user action | Verify with colleague |
| Can't print labels | Printer offline | Check connections |
| | Wrong printer selected | Select correct printer |
| Temperature alert | Door left open | Close door immediately |
| | Equipment failure | Notify supervisor |

### 13.2 System Error Messages

| Error Code | Meaning | Action |
|------------|---------|--------|
| ERR-001 | Session expired | Re-login |
| ERR-002 | Permission denied | Contact supervisor |
| ERR-003 | Record not found | Check reference number |
| ERR-004 | Duplicate entry | Verify if already processed |
| ERR-005 | Network timeout | Retry operation |
| ERR-006 | Validation failed | Check required fields |
| ERR-007 | Database error | Contact IT |

**à¦¬à¦¾à¦‚à¦²à¦¾:**

## 14. Support

### 14.1 Getting Help

**Support Channels:**

| Channel | Contact | When to Use |
|---------|---------|-------------|
| **Help Desk** | Extension 888 | Technical issues |
| **Warehouse Manager** | 017XXXXXXXX | Operational questions |
| **IT Support** | it@smartdairybd.com | System errors |
| **WhatsApp Support** | 017XXXXXXXX | Quick queries |
| **On-site Support** | Visit IT office | Hardware issues |

**When Reporting Issues:**
1. Note exact error message
2. Take screenshot if possible
3. Describe steps that led to issue
4. Note time when issue occurred
5. Provide your employee ID

### 14.2 Training Resources

**Available Training:**

| Training | Format | Duration |
|----------|--------|----------|
| New User Orientation | Classroom | 4 hours |
| System Refresher | Online | 1 hour |
| Cold Chain Certification | Classroom + Practical | 8 hours |
| Safety Training | Classroom | 4 hours |
| Scanner Training | Hands-on | 30 minutes |

**Training Schedule:**
- Contact HR or Training Lead
- Monthly refresher sessions
- On-demand for new features

### 14.3 Document Updates

**Version Control:**
- This document is version controlled
- Check document header for current version
- Major changes communicated via email
- Updates posted on staff notice board

**Feedback:**
- Submit suggestions to training@smartdairybd.com
- Include specific section references
- Describe improvement needed
